TITLE      Gamma-Ray Production Cross Sections in Multiple        14162001    3 
           Channels for Neutron-Induced Reaction on 48Ti for En   14162001    4 
           = 1 to 200 MeV                                         14162001    5 
AUTHOR     (D.Dashdorj,G.E.Mitchell,J.A.Becker,U.Agvaanluvsan,    14162001    6 
           L.A.Bernstein,W.Younes,P.E.Garrett,M.B.Chadwick,       14162001    7 
           M.Devlin,N.Fotiades,T.Kawano,R.O.Nelson)               14162001    8 
INSTITUTE  (1USALRL,1USANCS,1USATNL,1CANGUE,1USALAS)              14162001    9 
REFERENCE  (J,NSE,157,65,2007) Main reference.                    14162001   10 
           #doi:10.13182/NSE07-A2713                              14162001   11 
           (R,UCRL-TR-209474,2005) Reference used in superseded   14162001   12

           (C,2004SANTA,1,1035,2004) Conference presentation.     14162001   14

FACILITY   (LINAC,1USALAS) Weapons Neutron Research facility      14162001   16 
           WNR at the Los Alamos Neutron Science Center LANSCE    14162001   17 
INC-SOURCE (SPALL) Neutrons are produced by bombarding a natural  14162001   18 
           tungsten target with the 800-MeV pulsed proton beam    14162001   19 
           from the LANSCE linac. Neutrons with energies ranging  14162001   20 
           from a few keV to nearly 800 MeV are produced.         14162001   21 
           Beam-hardening material ~1.5 cm of lead was placed     14162001   22 
           in the neutron flight path, and charged particles      14162001   23 
           were swept from the flight line by permanent magnets   14162001   24 
SAMPLE     (22-TI-48,ENR=0.9981) 3.3 g of TiO2 enriched to        14162001   25 
           99.81% 48Ti in the form of a 2.4-cm-diam disk          14162001   26 
DETECTOR   (HPGE)The gamma rays were detected with the GEANIE     14162001   27 
           spectrometer, located 20.34 m from the neutron         14162001   28 
           source on the 60-deg right flight path.                14162001   29 
           The GEANIE spectrometer consisted of 11                14162001   30 
           planar and fifteen ~20% to 25% HPGe coaxial            14162001   31 
           detectors. All of the planar detectors and 9 of the    14162001   32 
           coaxial detectors were equipped with Compton           14162001   33 
           suppression shields. The detectors were situated at    14162001   34 
           a distance of 14 cm from the the scattering sample     14162001   35 
METHOD     (TOF,GSPEC) The detection time of gamma rays           14162001   36 
           produced by neutrons interacting with the sample was   14162001   37 
           used to calculate the TOF of the neutrons relative     14162001   38 
           to the micropulse time, measured by g-flash detection. 14162001   39 
MONITOR    Fission chamber with 235,238U foils, located 2 m       14162001   40 
           upstream from the GEANIE spectrometer. Fission         14162001   41 
           chamber events were used to determine the neutron flux.14162001   42
